What we think, as we are very few people with same interst which get familar with this coin, just a few month ago is not the case... statically or logically...
For see the future of market trough your ice ball, you should creat or buy first.
But before that, for invest on market like wise old man (buffet) You can do this:
1_ read every thing about it... from nytimes article to some unknown blogger idea.
2_ calculate the whole Coin share, rate of production, target group, rate of interst... every thing...
3_ finaly you can guess! If i buy this mana coin is this good or not?
We are in 2021 pandemic... you cant trust market movement, trend... because simply we do not know after pandemi how market react to the CC, how gov decide about regulation and income, and many thing else... but you can trust your feeling and bet on few new coin which will be raise in recent few month because right now people have fate on CC... NO MATTER WHAT. but, honestly it like gumbbling.
The other method, you can calculate price is this:
1_ rule one... trend is your only friend. trust it.
2_ you are "following" the trend... do not think about proficy of market movement.
3_ use real time frame data, then try diffrent module to calculate the market trend, test them and if there was a good fortune on that, run it... make money. 
There is a 3th way also...
Using real time market analysing bot which mining data from all over network, then convert this data to number which have meaningfull relation to price... 
For example, the most basic and dummy way to estimate bitcoin price movement is:
1_ Create a chart from search history of bitcoin and related keyword on google.
2_ inspect "ads price" on diffrent social network and if you could make a data chart about them... 
3_ use statical analysis to find relation between this data or other chart you are using with hisoricaly price market... 
4_ use a very fast and sencetive triger mechanism beside a classic andicator to verify the historicaly price detection...
5_ if it was succesfull, try diffrent method to find the best efficent point on price chart... then run your program... its your ice ball.
But in the end of day, no matter what you do, its just gambling... you just try to put your bid when you are not drunk, calculate odds of winning, inspect the other player movement... but there is a chance your fullhouse card lose to core card...

    [06.04.2021 09:00:12 UTC-05:00] Deleted Account
I will leave this group today as I found some unpleasant facts about this puzzle. 

I encourage everyone to think twice before trying to find solutions. The puzzle is badly designed. There are serious flaws and this comes from someone who has worked with _hush hush_ data all his life. 

Just two examples.  I have  found many more. 

1. When OP_data (part of the puzzle) was added in TX for the 'causality' brain wallet, it was done on the compressed side - 1Jqq37KkZEt4F3Dt6qXdtyiMEFBBdawbkJ – The puzzle makers did not even check to see that the uncompressed address was already created in 2013. I guess they found out after the puzzle was made public [this alone adds unplanned and unnecessary confusion and for me it shows bad design]

2.  You can read all the public OP_data directly on the blockchain instead of going through whatever phase and whatever ciphers [this was also unplanned] How? Just use a blockchain parser and search for 47534d472e (ASCI for their website). Sample at:   blockchain [dot] info/block/000000000000000000078fbc77e0c5e2b10ade8880a265c140e6e36d29b2da29?format=hex ] --- this is only for a single block but of course it's all there...

3.  Moreover, the January 2020 hint was announced as THE LAST hint, see chat history.  And yet, others were posted after. This can only prove that they realized this puzzle cannot be solved without them frequently interfering in the solving process. My sincere advice to them: please, do not provide any more clues to these poor people.  These clues [which are different puzzles altogether!] cannot help unexperienced solvers with their thinking process. And the users who think they have understood the hints just because they got onto the next phase they will be in for quite a surprise. 

4.  I am not interested in the actual prize. It will be unethical for me to actually claim it and it might have quite some negative consequences on me if I do so [and the word gets out]. I wanted to say nothing, but I can see so many are messaging me [please don’t] and struggling and it’s all because of a bad design not because the puzzle is hard - in popular layman terms. I was here to send a professional warning to all those spending too much time on this – it's a nice try but it was not built well and you will waste more time than you think because the construct is flawed. 

Just ask yourself: what if there were no clues at all? None. Just the puzzle. For how long people would still be stuck? Years perhaps. Why? Because you NEED clues and that is bad design.  

Do something better with your time. Have fun, read and work hard. Be kind to others, it will pay off. 

As for this puzzle, even if you get to a so called final stage trust me, you will hit the biggest wall of all and you will be quite disappointed. 
 
Adios! Exiting the channel soon …👋🏻

@SoWut [https://t.me/SoWut]  - There is one recent question someone asked,  would be great if you could answer. Regarding this part: B -> ((BV80605001911AP)- (sqrt(-1)))^2.  The Intel part number in that hint is for an i5. Using the value of 5i there results in an answer of -16. 

However, the Safenet Netherlands coordinates (https://www.google.com/maps/place/51%C2%B052'12.4%22N+4%C2%B025'18.2%22E/@51.8701111,4.4217222,17z/data=!3m1!4b1!4m4!3m3!8m2!3d51.8701111!4d4.4217222?entry=ttu) have 52 in that spot (originally 25 as the coords are reversed.) So is it possible that someone originally meant to write this and it was transcribed wrong: -((5i) + (sqrt(-1)))^2 - which would have equaled 25?

The concern of course, is whether there are any other small typos that could prevent us from advancing to the next stage...  any thoughts?

    [26.03.2024 11:59:17 UTC-05:00] MRG
Roses are not naturally black because they do not produce the pigment necessary to create black petals. The color of a flower is determined by its genetic makeup and the presence of specific pigments. While there are some varieties of roses that appear very dark, such as deep red or purple, true black roses do not exist in nature. However, horticulturists have been able to create "black" roses by breeding and manipulating the flower's genetic makeup to produce darker pigments, resulting in varieties that appear very close to black

>>> [11.07.2024 14:29:17 UTC-05:00] Jrk Bgrt

    [11.07.2024 18:12:13 UTC-05:00] RB
well... (but) no ;)
as written 'the header' is: 71 a4 49
the first 2 bytes in binary:
0111 0001 1010 0100 [written in 4byte blocks]
after studying the wikipedia articles about qr code and ECI i would interpret these as:
0111:  ECI indicator
0001 1010: ECI Assignment number = 26 -> UTF-8
0100: binary encoding

49 [hex] -> 73 [decimal] is the length of the following string

the 'footer': 00 ec 11 ec
00: to me is a null termination
'ec' and '11' are the 'fillers' used in qr codes

There is no clear roadmap, no structured hints — nothing except the original image and the AES blocks. For those who have just joined this fascinating challenge, it is very difficult and unclear what is actually going on.

    [03.03.2026 15:29:50 UTC-05:00] Flo Sku

What more do you want? He’s not going to hand us the solution on a silver platter, that’s the whole point of a puzzle.

Personally, I don’t want a hint that lets someone crack it in two hours. That would honestly drive me crazy. I love the rush I get every time I follow a new lead and it actually makes sense. Even when it goes nowhere, it still feels like I’m getting a bit closer each time. I hope the puzzle keeps going. It’s making me learn new things every day.

Also, in the dbbi string, you can replace the B and BE, in order and by counting them, with prime numbers (d B[2] B[3] i B[5] f B[7]…). This matches the blue and yellow squares in the puzzle image (counter clockwise, B for blue and BE for yellow), with one extra prime number (73) in place of the very light grey square (fefefe). That fits the creator’s hint "yellow blue primes" but it seems we haven’t found how to go further yet.

    [13.04.2026 11:25:35 UTC-05:00] X
All Good Things Come To An End.

The End of GSMG Our 9 Year Chaos Tour Is Officially Over, But the Stories Stay… Forever.


Hey legends.
After almost nine years of pure madness, caffeine overdoses and more red candles than any human should endure, it is time to turn the lights off.
But before we do, grab a drink, get comfortable and let me tell you the whole stupid story straight from the idiots who lived it. It all started in 2017. JRK was visiting Sydney with the better half. Instead of playing tourist like a normal person, he locked himself in a living room for nine straight days. Zero high-end programming skills. Just Siemens PLC code, some HTML, Quake 3 scripting and a bit of Pascal. He built the entire bot from scratch as one single terrifying, never-ending script. No functions. No classes. Just pure chaos and hope.
On June 10th at around 8:30 in the morning, the first order actually hit Poloniex servers. It somehow worked, albeit that the ATH of rising markets wasn’t overwritten, thus we started by selling for a loss. The very first name for this script was MR. ROIbot. And right there on that same day, d0d was already in the mix (he already knew infrastructure expert Darky, too). Greengras hooked us up with the very first server space, and the experienced algotrading coder Bloctite joined shortly after and basically saved our lives by rewriting the ENTIRE codebase (Python plus Cython, and currently basically bug-free). 1 idiot and 3 professionals with complementary skills, a host, and one big stupid dream. What could go wrong?
The reason it all started? JRK and d0d had just used another bot run by a scammer called fuzzyhobbit and thought nope. We are doing this the right way for everybody. That disrespect for the old banking system? Still burns to this day. And that is literally where Globally Supporting My Generation came from. An old friend's group name was reused and suddenly became a mission. Give the power back to the little guy.
A little later, JRK got inspired by other crypto puzzles and spent two sloppy days throwing one together. Full of grammatical mistakes and zero polish. Sorry about the mental damage. That thing is still running, and we are keeping it alive. In 40 years, he might admit he forgot how to solve it himself. The torture continues. You are welcome.
The early days were absolutely mental. Within the first few days, we were already handling around 8 million dollars in value. The market analyser and trading engine we built back then were absolute beasts; they’ve been running nearly flawlessly ever since.
We wanted to offer a proper high-end portfolio management tool to the little guy at stupidly low prices. That was always the point. (And yes, now in 2026, AI can do the same thing in one shot if you’re a prompt genius with decent subscriptions and setups. Thanks for nothing, future.)
Here is the part nobody likes to say out loud.
We never paid ourselves a single cent of salary in all these years. We had exactly one team dinner funded by GSMG. One. That is it. (Admittedly, it was a very nice dinner.) Every single subscription went straight into upgrades for Jeff Bezos's wife's latest mega yacht, and maybe even her youth.
We had some absolutely legendary moments together.
Besides the community chat banter that still makes us cry laugh at 3 am.
Boat rides with the first bunnies.
Accidentally melting an exchange by ramping our API call limit parameter times one hundred (sorry again, lads).
Some of you lost money. We know the classic move. Coin moons set the bot to 220% aggression at the top coin dumps, blame the bot. Standard crypto rite of passage. But we also saw some of you catch beautiful flash crashes and turn minutes into multiple BTC. Those wins still make us giggle like little kids.
The ride was always about getting YOU rich. Hehe. We are not here for the money; we are here for the tech. Aren’t we all? We actually meant the first part.

>>> [13.04.2026 11:25:35 UTC-05:00] Jrk Bgrt 13.04.2026 11:21:41
So why are we stopping?
To run a bot like this in 2026, you need a ridiculous amount of compute. Our market analyser is a proper cruncher which deals with big data, all on the fly (big data by definition, fyi). It crunches numbers every microsecond, year in year out. To stay competitive, it costs a fortune. The whole setup only really makes financial sense for the big whales and UHNWIs on the highest tier. Running these calculations for the shrimps is literally killing us financially. The other subscription levels are not enough to keep it +EV. We tried. We crunched the numbers until our eyes hurt. Time to be honest and do the inevitable.
We try to be a bit ghostly, but we are definitely not ghosting you. Here is what we are doing for you right now.
The dashboard will stay open for a few days, and we’ll make sure you can retrieve your history. Also, our terms and conditions state that we have to return all funds from the last 2 weeks. We’ll make that 6 weeks instead. So, please stop sending us funds for your subscriptions.
We are not deleting the code. We are still figuring out what to do with it (maybe open source it, maybe something else, sell it to w/e company, fund or individual. We will let you know soon, or you may contact us, of course.
Your personal data was always kept to bank security grade plus standards. It will be deleted and will never be included in a sale (might that ever happen).
So thank you.
Thank you for trusting a bunch of idiots with a dream. Thank you for the memes, the rage messages, the wins, the losses and every single story you shared. This ride was never about us getting rich. It was about getting YOU rich in a world that needed it.
The lights are going off, but the story? That one lives forever.
Stay dangerous out there, stack sats and may your future entries always be better than your exits.
With love, zero regrets,
JRK, d0d, Darky, Bloctite, and the remaining GSMG crew.
P.S. The puzzle is still unsolved. We are watching from the sidelines with an infinite amount of popcorn without giving any hints - we hope that this will remain community-maintained, as the URL might vanish. 👀
P.P.S. Don’t worry about us; we’ve been busy with many non-GSMG things in the meantime. Who knows, you might enjoy some of the services/products we worked on somewhere in your life. You may find us in digital delivery systems for the entertainment and racing industry, automobile global human transport services, educational platforms, card game, logistics, data analyses, music-related entertainment, and many more.
